Other abbreviations and notes

[Diry]  - Directory Assistance Exchange - presently, no access to directory
          assistance exists from Canada. AT&T reportedly has a system which
          allows connection to the appropriate operators of the various
          islands involved. Within the Caribbean itself, this may be used
          for directory assistance within a territory (not necessarily over
          the entire 809 Caribbean region).

???     - means that the exchange was found to be active, but that its
          location was not determined as of yet; this could be a switch
          misprogramming, or a forthcoming exchange
(T-PT)  - reserved for phone testing
(950S)  - reserved for alternate long distance service
(976S)  - reserved for special announcements services

        0    international access (i.e. use 00+ for international calls)
             formerly local rate (02 time, 03 weather, 07 repair, 08 national
             enquiries), but those codes moved to 60 or 68, 11/1/1991, to

33  France
    [France moved to 8 digit numbers; Paris area has an area code of
     (1); the rest of France has no area code, just the 8 digit number,
     presumably beginning with the other codes listed below. Nigel Allen
     reported that France will change its numbering plan yet again to
     accommodate growth. - djcl]
    [Apparently the move to 8 digits was done Oct. 19-20 or 26-27, 1985.]
    (domestically, 05 + 6 digits "numero vert" [green number] toll-free
     services; 05 to change to 0800?)
    [At present, domestic long distance access code is 16,
     international access code is 19. In 1995, the numbering plan
     is expected to change so that domestic long distance access code
     will be 0, while international access code will be 00. The area
     codes from 1995 will be set up as follows:
        1 Ile-de-France (Metro Paris)
        2 Northeast France
        3 Southeast France
        4 Southwest France
        5 Northwest France (notice 05 above)
        6(?) mobile
        -- 1 thru 5 courtesy Erik Thomas Mueller (etm@email.teaser.com)]

Date: Fri, 8 Apr 94 18:26:47 +0200
From: Thierry Samama <Thierry.Samama@aar.alcatel-alsthom.fr>

Hi there. Since I didn't know who to send this to, I sent it to the three of you. Upon reading your listings for zone 3, I realized that the French listing was not as detailed as it could be. Here is a list of French STDs, for potential inclusion, if you see fit, in the telecom archives. Feel free to edit the explanation, I realize it is a little convoluted, but it's Friday evening...

Best regards,
Thierry.


33 France
[France is currently divided into two dialing zones: the Paris region (zone 1), and the rest of France (zone 9). Within a zone, subscribers all have an 8D number, where the first four digits identify the local exchange and the last four digits identify the subscriber.]
+-----------+-------------+-------------+-------------+
| To dial   | from zone 1 | from zone 9 | from abroad |
+-----------+-------------+-------------+-------------+
| to zone 1 | 8D          | 16 1 8D     | 33 1 8D     |
+-----------+-------------+-------------+-------------+
| to zone 9 | 16 8D       | 8D          | 33 8D       |
+-----------+-------------+-------------+-------------+

In zone 1, the first digit of the local exchange number has geographical significance:
3	Yvelines, Val d'Oise
4	Paris, Hauts-de-Seine, Seine-St-Denis, Val-de-Marne
5	Paris
6	Seine-et-Marne, Essonne

In zone 9, the first two digits of the local exchange number have geographical significance, and they identify a "departement", which is somewhere between a county and a state.
20	Nord (Lille)
21	Pas-de-Calais
22	Somme
23	Aisne
24	Ardennes
25	Aube, Haute-Marne

35	Seine-Maritime

37	Eure-et-Loir
38	Loiret

4	Oise

      change to the standard 0 on 12th October 1996 at 00.00. All area codes
      will change as well, the total number of 75 codes changes down to 13
      (the so called telecommunication areas) - the areas are almost the same
      as the provinces of the country:

Luxembourg is a small country where STD/routing codes as such are not
required. The locations of telephone numbers (4-6 digits, variable
even within a city or region) can be determined by checking the first
digit or two, however. The following list, then, indicates what
region the initial portion of the telephone number represents.
The first digit generally identifies the region:
2          Luxembourg (city)
3          area surrounding Luxembourg (city)
4          Luxembourg (city)
5          southwest
60, 65-69  southeast
61-64      west
7          east
8          north central
9          far north

Date:     Sat, 26 Aug 95 10:06:10 EDT
From:     cmoore@ARL.MIL
Subject:  zone.4.uk.44.detailed

DCCL - World Numbering Zone 4 - European countries (part 2: +44 (UK))
21 June 1995
Inquiries: contact cmoore@ARL.MIL or djcl@io.org
---------------------------------------------------------------------------
44 United Kingdom (includes England, Scotland, Wales, Northern Ireland)
    [London, formerly area code 1, split in 1990 to form 71 (inner London)
     and 81 (outer London). In UK, area codes are normally merged instead
     of being split.]

    [The "phONEday" change to area code system is expected to be complete
     16 April 1995 as 1 is prepended to almost all area codes (except
     for non-geographic codes like 800 (within UK: 0800), 898 (domestically,
     0898) and mobile, and except for a few cities), to allow for new area
     codes in the future. A permissive dialing period began August 1994.
     Codes in this list have been changed accordingly.]

    [Extra information on changing codes courtesy BT via Richard
     Ross-Langley (rrl@minfo.demon.co.uk) and William H. Blunn
     (bone@bone.demon.co.uk) via uk.telecom newsgroup.]

        The following codes have NO leading 0 (used within UK):
        150   Operator
        155   Repair Service
        192   Directory Enquiry (directory assistance)
        999   emergency (to be replaced by 112)

        The following codes DO add a leading 0 within UK:

        0      international access (as of 16 April 1995)
        066    [rarely used premium services code; domestically 0066]
        077    [rarely used premium services code; domestically 0077]
        1      London (replaced by 71 & 81); next digit was of form N
        10     international access (becomes 0 on 16 April 1995)
        113    Leeds (was 532; 2+6D old local #, 16 April 1995)
        114    Sheffield (was 742; 2+6D old local #, 16 April 1995)

49 (Federal Republic of) Germany (former West and East Germany)
   Before unification, this code had West Germany only.  The
   former East Germany was absorbed here with city codes start-
   ing with 3, previously unassigned except for Berlin. This took
   effect 15th April 1992, though at the time some countries reported
   that +37 was still necessary for the former East Germany.

   Now, codes in the form +37x are assigned to some former Soviet
   republics. See the World Zone 3 listings (+37x) for details.

   Postal code, if available, follows city name; currently
   using only the postal codes of the former West Germany.

   Some cities have more than one code; and one code could cover
   more than one city.

   Neither area codes nor prefixes have a fixed length.  Area codes
   are 2-4 digits in the western part and 2-5 digits in the eastern
   part (3xxxx) of Germany. All subscriber numbers are 3-7 digits
   and up to 8 digits for PBX. The area code and the subscriber num-
   ber together are not longer than 10 digits. Most 3 digit area codes
   were of the form zX1, where z is the ZVSt (central switching office).
   But the number of exceptions increased over the years: 202, 203, 208,
   209, 212, 214, 228, 234, 335, 340, 345, 355, 365, 375, 385, 395, 906.
   The most exceptions of this rule are within the ZVSt 2 because there
   are a lot of large cities and within the ZVSt 3 because that covers a
   large region (the eastern part of Germany). The area code z11 is usually
   the area code for the city where the ZVSt is located, except for cities
   which got 2 digit area codes: 30, 40, 69, 89.

   ZVSt 2 Du:sseldorf
   ZVSt 3 Berlin (former East German areas - effective 15 April 1992)
   ZVSt 4 Hamburg
   ZVSt 5 Hannover
   ZVSt 6 Frankfurt am Main
   ZVSt 7 Stuttgart
   ZVSt 8 Mu:nchen
   ZVSt 9 Nu:rnberg

    Much of the following update is courtesy of Thomas Diessel
    (diessel@informatik.unibw-muenchen.de)

        Notes from Ben Kinchant:
        "New Zealand is in the process of changing its area codes and local
        numbers.  Before this process started, each free calling area
        had its own area code, the area code being between 1 and 6 digits
        and with the local number being between 3 and 7 digits!
        "The process (which is called NZ Phone number Update) is changing
        all numbers to seven digits, and reducing the number of area
        codes from 80 to 5.
        "The updating/changing of numbers should be finished by the end of
        1992, with the bulk of number having been changed this year [1991]..."

From: cmoore@ARL.MIL
Date: Wed, 10 May 95 12:45:25 EDT
Subject:  zone.7

DCCL - World Numbering Zone 7 - former USSR territory, including CIS nations
9 May 1995
Inquiries: contact cmoore@ARL.MIL or djcl@io.org
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------

7   Former Soviet Union (including republics in the Commonwealth of
    Independent States), before some republics changed codes. Many
    nations never recognized 1940 seizure of the Baltic republics,
    which are now using new country codes (see below).

    [If asterisk appears at end of line containing a 3-digit city code,
    add '22' or '2', respectively, before a 5 or 6 digit telephone number.
    Otherwise, add '00' or '0', respectively. This note was written 19
    Sept. 1990; later-arriving entries will be marked "&" if such add-on
    information is unknown.

    [31 Oct 1992: new information from OAG Travel Planner was found for
    these nations. Individual republics are listed now; any question mark
    after a republic name indicates that this is probably which country
    the code belongs to, but was not confirmed.

    [30 Apr 1993: some nations formerly in country code 7 now have service
    under new country codes. These are Lithuania (+370), Latvia (+371),
    Estonia (+372) and Moldova (+373), all in the European zone 3 (see
    that file for detailed listings of these nations).

    [27 Feb 1995: Belarus will use +375 and Ukraine +380 effective
    16 April 1995, as these nations withdraw from the +7 country code.
    Azerbaijan was assigned country code +994, but implementation
    appears to be limited (mentioned in BT's phone books in the UK).

    [29 Apr 1995:
    * Armenia changes to +374, effective 1 May 1995; permissive dialing
      with +7 until 1 July 1995.
    * Belarus +375 has permissive dialing with +7 until some unknown point
      in 1997.
    * Ukraine has permissive dialing with +7 for approximately six months
      following the 16 Apr 1995 activation of +380.
    * Georgia has been assigned +995; details of any changeover from +7
      are unknown at this point.]

Note 1 (courtesy Jason Childers, notes added in brackets where new
        codes were found):

Date: 26 Feb 92 11:50:00 EST
From: childeja@UDAVXB.OCA.UDAYTON.EDU (Jason Childers)
Subject: Name Game in the CIS

Now that the Soviet Union (USSR, CCCP) is non-existent, the republics
have decided to change the names of some of their cities back to their
pre-Soviet titles.  Here is a list of names which {Time Magazine}
published last month, some of which are stated in the Telecom Archives
file ZONE.7 as having city codes:

[notice 2 occurrences of Ordzhonikidze, in Russia and in Georgia]

Old name                        New Name                Code

Leninakan, Armenia              Kumayri or Giumri       7 885 69
Kirovabad, Azerbaijan           Gyandzha                7 895
Minsk, Byelorussia              Mensk, Belarus          7 017   %%
Gegechkori, Georgia             Martvili
Makharadze, Georgia             Ozurgeti
Ordzhonikidze, Georgia          Kharagouli
Tsakhaya, Georgia               Senaki
Tsulukidze, Georgia             Khoni
Frunze, Kirghizia               Bishkek, Kyrgyzstan     7 331
Rybachye, Kirghizia             Issyk-Kul, Kyrgyzstan
Moldavia                        Moldova
Andropov, Russia                Rybinsk                 7 085 37
Brezhnev, Russia                Naberezhnye Chelny      7 843 9, 7 855
Chernenko, Russia               Sharypovo
Georgiu-Dezh, Russia            Liski
Gorky, Russia                   Nizhni(i) Novgorod      7 831
Kirov, Russia                   Vyatka                  7 833
Kuibyshev, Russia               Samara                  7 846
Kalinin                         Tver                    7 082
Leningrad, Russia               St Petersburg           7 812
Ordzhonikidze, Russia           Vladikarkaz             7 867
Sverdlovsk, Russia              Yekaterinburg           7 343
Ustinov, Russia                 Izhevsk                 7 341
Voroshilovgrad, Russia          Lugansk                [7 064?]
Zagorsk, Russia                 Sergiev Posad           7 254
Lvov, The Ukraine               Lviv, Ukraine           7 032    %%
Voroshilovgrad, The Ukraine     Lugansk, Ukraine        7 064    %%
Zhdanov, The Ukraine            Mariupol, Ukraine       7 062 9  %%
[added by CGM from another source:]
Ulyanovsk, Russia               Simbirsk                7 842

Any edits and amendments would be appreciated.

Does anybody know if Kaliningrad (the little oblast north of Poland
and west of either Estonia or Lithuania (sorry, don't have a map next
to me) is going back to being known as Ko:ningsberg?

Jason Childers <childeja@udavxb.oca.udayton.edu>

Note 2:

(courtesy Carl Moore)

These change only a vowel (mind you, Russian uses the Cyrillic
alphabet instead of the one we use).  How does this compare to
the changes such as Peking-to-Beijing in China?
Minsk --> Mensk
Lvov --> Lviv

I also notice Kirghizia --> Kyrgyzstan.  Nit-picking change
in the "Kirghiz" spelling; yes, I also see the "ia" and "stan"
endings.

Kaliningrad (Ko:nigsberg being the name it had when part of
East Prussia in Germany) is in an enclave which is part of
the Russian republic but which borders Poland and Lithuania
(you have to go through Lithuania and Byelorussia, now called
Belarus, to reach the rest of the Russian republic).

Yekaterinburg (see notes below regarding Sverdlovsk) has also
been spelled without the leading Y; I'm sure this is due to
transliteration from the Cyrillic alphabet.

--------------------------------------------------------------------------

Note 3:

Tolyatti (+7 848), also spelled Toliatti, is apparently named for former
Italian Communist party leader Palmiro Togliatti(?). This name may have
been changed, as is known to have happened to many other cities named for
Communists (and not just in the former USSR):

Leningrad, Russia
Stalingrad, Russia
 (became Volgograd long ago in "de-Stalinization" program under Khrushchev)
Andropov, Russia
Brezhnev, Russia
Chernenko, Russia
Kalinin, Russia
Sverdlovsk, Russia
 (became Yekaterinburg, the name it had before the Bolshevik revolution
 and when deposed Tsar Nicholas II and his family were murdered there in
 1918; according to "Nicholas and Alexandra", Jacob Sverdlov headed the
 Soviet cabinet and arranged those murders)
Ulyanovsk, Russia (Ulyanov was Lenin's real last name)
Leninakan, Armenia
Karl-Marx-Stadt (became Chemnitz), in the former East Germany
Wilhelm-Pieck-Stadt (became Guben), in the former East Germany
Titograd (became Podgorica), in the former Yugoslavia
Gottwaldov (became Zlin), in the former Czechoslovakia

89  spare

Note: 886 is not assigned to Taiwan by the CCITT.  The CCITT notes that
the People's Republic of China has assigned 866 to Taiwan.  88x codes
are not to be assigned until all the other 8xx codes are gone.
(PRC and the United Nations claim that Taiwan is part of PRC.)
The usage of 886 to reach Taiwan is ex-officio, though recognized by
the statement that 88x codes are the last to be assigned.
All the 87x codes are assigned to the Maritime Mobile Service.

China list was sent by David Leibold from a 1991 English-language
business directory of China.




Date: Sat, 29 Apr 95 12:56 EDT
From: dleibold@gvc.com (Dave Leibold)

DCCL - World Numbering Zone 9 - West and South Asia, including Middle East
18 April 1995
Inquiries: please contact cmoore@ARL.MIL or djcl@io.org

90  Turkey
    [Turkey went from six (2+4) to seven digits (3+4) local phone
    numbers c.1988, at which time Ankara went from 41 to 4.

    Before the city codes were revamped (see below), the Turkish-occupied
    part of Cyprus was sometimes noted as having country code 905, i.e.
    90 (Turkey) + 5 (area code for Cyprus points); this apparently affected
    all city codes which started with 5, except for 51.

    From Serdar Boztas (serdar@fawlty8.eng.monash.edu.au), November 1993:

    "The telephone numbering system in Turkey has recently been revamped.
    There used to be more than 5000 local area codes of varying lengths
    (one to five digits to the best of my knowledge) with correspondingly
    varying local number lengths (seven to three digits).

    "The new system is based on 77 three-digit area codes for provinces and
    seven digit local phone numbers. Istanbul is the exception and it gets
    three area codes (I think two for the European side and one for the
    Asian side).

    "0 will be the long distance dialing prefix while the international
    dialing prefix will be 00."

    Local numbers in most areas were also changed in conjunction with the
    numbering plan that took effect 1 August 1993. A list of the new area
    codes with the associated local numbering changes can be found at
    http://www.metu.edu.tr/misc/phone-codes.html (courtesy soc.culture.turkish
    FAQ (sctfaq@mistik.express.net) and Jean-Bernard Condat)

    If a former area code is indicated, this is for the major centre
    in the new area code's district. The new area codes will also
    replace former area codes other than the primary one mentioned.]

[6(3) means area code is 6, telephone numbers within that area code
 begin with 3, but 3 is not part of the area code as such - info
 from an Israeli directory. Additional info courtesy David Lemson
 (lemson@uiuc.edu, for area code 56 info) and Dr. Josh Backon
 (backon@vms.huji.ac.il) for update on area code 7]

no leading 0 is used before these numbers (based on information from
Jerusalem 1993 directory):

        177  toll free, home direct (e.g. 177+610 2727 is Australia direct)
        188  overseas calling operator
